Telegram Bureau Chief Wu Baofeng Discusses the Issue of Joint Establishment of Postal and Telegraph Offices 136

Dispatching Personnel to Inspect the Actual Situation First

Drafting Methods to be Submitted to the Ministry for Approval

Shanghai Telegram Bureau Chief Wu Baofeng recently went to Beijing and has already returned to Shanghai. A reporter from the Central News Agency specifically interviewed Mr. Wu. According to him, the details of his trip to Beijing are as follows:

Telegram Bureau Reorganization Plan 137

Mr. Wu first stated that after taking office, he drafted opinions on the internal reorganization plan and submitted them to the Ministry for approval. During this trip to Beijing, he personally presented the plan to Minister Zhu. Mr. Wu believes that the existing buildings of the Telegram Bureau are inconvenient for business operations and intends to rebuild them. Minister Zhu stated that the Ministry of Communications is currently planning to consolidate the telecommunications agencies under its jurisdiction in Shanghai into one location to facilitate operations and achieve synergistic effects. Shanghai is a vital transportation hub, and its industrial and commercial prosperity is unmatched in the country. This plan seems to need to be realized as soon as possible. Therefore, the issue of rebuilding the Telegram Bureau will be addressed after the Ministry of Communications decides on the overall plan.

Issue of Paying Security Deposits 138

Mr. Wu further mentioned the issue of paying security deposits. The Ministry of Communications previously, in order to facilitate and expedite the procedures for telegram senders, required business firms and residents who frequently send telegrams to pay a certain amount of security deposit on a monthly basis. This security deposit is deposited by the Telegram Bureau with the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, which pays interest. This method can save telegram senders from the accounting complications each time they send a telegram and significantly speed up the process. The purpose of the Ministry of Communications' move is solely to provide convenience for merchants.

Joint Establishment of Postal and Telegraph Offices 139

Finally, Mr. Wu also discussed the issue of jointly establishing postal and telegraph offices. Although this is for the sake of saving costs for postal and telegraph agencies, it can also greatly benefit the people in practice. In the future, postal and telegraph offices in various locations will gradually seek joint establishment based on actual needs. In Shanghai, the Telegram Bureau will work with the Shanghai Postal Administration to dispatch personnel to inspect the actual situation of postal and telegraph offices of the third class and below. Then, considering the market conditions in each location, a plan for joint establishment will be drafted and submitted to the Ministry for approval, after which implementation can begin.

Ministry of Communications Dispatches Personnel to Austria to Study Postal Savings and Remittance 140

Recruitment Set for Six Regular Candidates and Four Alternates

Registration Starts on the 5th and Exams on June 1st

Since the Ministry of Communications launched postal savings and remittance services, the business has seen considerable progress. Postal savings and remittance is a specialized field. In order to cultivate talent in this area, the Ministry has decided to select trainees to study at the Austrian Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. To ensure seriousness, the Ministry will select qualified personnel through an examination before dispatching them. It is now reported that the training program and recruitment program have been finalized and announced by the Ministry of Communications. Registration will begin on March 5th and end on May 15th. The exam will be held in Beijing on June 1st. The original texts of the two programs are excerpted below:

Training Program Article 1: In order to cultivate specialized talent in savings and remittance, the Ministry selects trainees to study savings and remittance operations at the Austrian Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. Article 2: The number of trainees is six. Priority is given to current employees of the Postal Administration and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau who meet the qualifications, who may register for the exam. External recruitment is also conducted through an examination process. The recruitment procedures are specified in a separate program. Article 3: After non-bureau employees are admitted, they will first be sent by the two Administrations to designated domestic bureaus to study for a period of two months. Article 4: The examination qualifications for trainees stipulated in Article 2 are: having worked in the Postal Administration or the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau in the handling of reserve funds or exchange matters for more than three years. For non-bureau employees, the qualifications are: graduation from the economics or business department of a domestic or foreign university recognized by the Ministry of Education, having worked in a bank for more than three years, and proficiency in German or English. Article 5: The examination subjects are as follows: Chinese Language, German or English, Economics, Banking and Currency, Accounting, Insurance, and Remittance. Article 6: The training period is set at two years. During the training period, trainees may not change to another country or another subject without authorization. Article 7: The training subjects are as follows: Business Management, Accounting, Savings, Remittance, and Insurance. Article 8: During the training period, trainees who were originally employees of the two Administrations will receive their original salary, except for those with a monthly salary of less than 100 yuan, who will receive their original salary in full. Those with a salary of 100 yuan or more will receive half of their salary. If half of their salary is less than 100 yuan, they will still receive 100 yuan. In addition, they will receive a clothing allowance of 500 yuan, a travel allowance of 80 English pounds, and a monthly living allowance of 20 English pounds. The return travel allowance is the same. Trainees who are not employees of the two Bureaus will be considered employees of the Savings and Remittance Bureau from the date of admission and will receive a monthly allowance of 100 yuan. All other expenses are the same as for employees. Article 9: After completing the training period and returning to China, trainees have an obligation to serve in the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau for a period of not less than five years. Article 10: After being admitted, trainees should fill out a service application. Article 11: This program will be implemented from the date of publication.

Recruitment Program Article 1: This program is formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 2 of the Ministry of Communications' Program for Selecting Trainees to Study Savings and Remittance in Austria. Article 2: This examination will be conducted by the Examination Committee organized by the Ministry of Communications. Article 3: Anyone who meets one of the following qualifications may register with the Examination Committee: (A) Current employees of the Postal Administration and the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau who have been handling savings and remittance business for more than three years; (B) Graduates from the economics or business department of a domestic or foreign university recognized by the Ministry of Education who have worked in a bank for more than three years. When registering, applicants should submit a resume, supporting documents, and three recent half-length photos, and pay a registration fee of two yuan (those qualified under item A are exempt from the registration fee). After the review is completed, a notice will be published in the newspaper announcing the examination (unqualified applicants will be refunded the registration fee and supporting documents upon presentation of the receipt). Regardless of whether they are admitted or not, the registration fee will not be refunded. Article 4: The registration period is from March 5th to May 15th of this year. Late submissions will not be accepted. Article 5: Applicants should go to a doctor designated by the Ministry of Communications to undergo a physical examination from May 27th after reading the newspaper notice. Only after receiving a notice of passing the physical examination can they participate in the examination. Article 6: This examination is scheduled to be held in Nanjing on June 1st of this year. The examination location will be announced separately. Article 7: The examination subjects are as follows: Party Principles, Chinese Language, German or English, Economics, Banking and Currency, Accounting, Insurance, and Remittance. This examination is divided into written and oral tests. Those who pass the written test will be scheduled for an oral test. Those who fail the written test will not be allowed to participate in the oral test. Article 8: The number of candidates to be admitted for this examination is set at six regular candidates and four alternates. If a regular candidate does not come to complete the necessary procedures or report within the specified time limit after being admitted, the alternate may be substituted. If the level of the examinees is insufficient, the number of candidates to be admitted may be reduced or another examination may be scheduled. Article 9: Those who are admitted after the oral test should submit a letter of intent within five days and report to the Postal Administration or the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to await assignment for training. Article 10: Candidates should not solicit any personnel of the Ministry of Communications, the Postal Administration, or the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau in any way. Otherwise, once discovered, they will be refused the examination before the examination and their qualifications will be cancelled and replaced after the examination. Article 11: This program will be implemented from the date of publication.

Workers at the Meyer Silk Factory Plan to Organize a Strike Committee 146

Yesterday Sent a Letter to the General Manager Requesting the Withdrawal of the Wage Reduction Order

Workers at the Meyer Silk Weaving Factory have recently been facing a strike due to the factory's wage cuts. Various unions gathered yesterday to discuss organizing a strike committee and plan to petition Party and government agencies on a scheduled basis. The detailed circumstances are as follows:

Wage Reduction Circumstances According to the workers' statement yesterday, at 1:00 PM on the 2nd of this month, the factory directors of the first factory on Malang Road, the second factory on Jiaotong Road, the third and fourth factories on Jiaozhou Road (now merged), the fifth and sixth factories on Xietu Road, the seventh factory on Quzhenren Road, the eighth factory on Dapuqiao Road, and the ninth factory on Wenlin Road, and the tenth factory at Bashi Bridge, gathered the workers to make a speech, saying that the factory's output of woven products last year was better than in previous years, but since the beginning of the year, there have been no orders from various places, which proves that the sales of silk fabrics have been declining. In order to prevent unforeseen circumstances, the factory plans to slightly reduce salaries and wages. At 2:00 PM, each factory issued a notice to implement the wage reduction.

Workers' Resentment The total number of workers in Meyer factories is more than 4,000. Seeing this notice, they expressed their dissatisfaction. The factory had previously reduced all wages by 10% on July 1st of last year due to the decline in silk sales. At that time, in order to avoid increasing resentment between labor and capital, the workers did not argue. Unexpectedly, only half a year later, the capitalists cut wages again. With the exception of the warp factory's warp department, apprentices, and the dyeing and finishing factory on Luban Road, the workers in other departments have gone on strike one after another. The standard for wage reduction is to reduce existing wages to 85%. This year, the factory has reduced staff. Recently, it was also announced that monthly salaries above 26 yuan will be reduced appropriately.

Organize a Strike Committee After the workers in each factory went on strike one after another, the original trade union had been cancelled. Fearing that malicious elements would become active during the strike, representatives from each factory gathered yesterday morning to discuss the overall plan. It was decided that: (1) The wage level of the first half of 1933 should be restored. (2) A written petition should be submitted to the general manager requesting the withdrawal of the order. (3) If there is no result, a petition should be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau on a scheduled basis. (4) A strike committee should be established to facilitate negotiations.

Da Hing Ship and Xin Ping Ship Collide, Navigation Administration Bureau Sent Personnel to Inspect the Ships Yesterday 147

=Xin Ping Suffered More Damage, Sent Letter to Da Hing for Negotiations=

=The Issue of Responsibility Will Be Judged by the Collision Committee=

The Xincheng Shipping Company's Xin Ping ship and the Antong Shipping Company's Da Hing ship collided at 5:53 AM on the 4th of this month at the Wusongkou entrance while entering the port, both ships were damaged, with Xin Ping suffering more damage than Da Hing. Yesterday, the Navigation Administration Bureau sent ship inspectors to investigate and will make a fair judgment in accordance with the law. The details are as follows:

Entering Port at the Same Time The Xincheng Shipping Company's Xin Ping ship, located at 22 Hankou Road in this city, with a total tonnage of 3,200 tons, loaded 40,000 bags of salt from Haikou and transported them to Shanghai. It arrived at Wusongkou on the evening of the 3rd of this month. For safe navigation, it anchored and waited to enter the port the next morning. At the same time, the Antong Shipping Company's Da Hing ship, located at 220 Sichuan Road, with a total tonnage of 3,208 tons, loaded coal from Pukou and transported it to Shanghai. It also arrived at Wusongkou on the evening of the 3rd and anchored. The Xin Ping ship arrived at Wusongkou first and anchored in front of the Da Hing ship. At 5:50 AM on the 4th, both ships simultaneously raised their anchors and entered the port.

Collision While Avoiding the Ship When entering the port, the Xin Ping ship was in front of the Da Hing ship. When the Xin Ping ship was about to reach Wusongkou, it slowed down. The Da Hing ship increased its speed in the rear, intending to overtake. At that time, it was just dawn, and the navigation route was difficult to distinguish. At this time, there happened to be an oil tanker, which was said to belong to the Asiatic Petroleum Company, leaving Shanghai. The Da Hing ship wanted to avoid it, but due to the rapid tide, the bow of the Da Hing ship collided with the side of the Xin Ping ship's third and fourth cabins. After applying the brakes, the oil tanker left the port as usual.

Both Were Damaged The third and fourth cabins of the Xin Ping ship were struck and a hole was created. The rivets and iron plates were damaged. Fortunately, it was above the waterline and there was no major problem. It immediately sailed to the Jinliyuan Wharf, Huangpu River floating buoys number three and four, and docked. The bow of the Da Hing ship was slightly damaged by iron rivets. It sailed to the Beipiao Wharf and docked. After inspection by the shipowner, the damage was very minor. However, the Xin Ping ship suffered more serious damage, and it was reported that water had entered the salt艙.

Ship Inspection Yesterday The Xincheng Shipping Company submitted a report to the Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications regarding the collision of the Xin Ping ship and requested an investigation. At 10:00 AM yesterday, Wang Xinyuan, a ship inspector from the Navigation Administration Bureau, first went to the Jinliyuan floating buoy to inspect the Xin Ping ship, and then went to the Beipiao Wharf to inspect the Da Hing ship. The Xincheng Shipping Company sent a letter to the Antong Shipping Company yesterday detailing the damage to the Xin Ping ship for negotiation.

Fair Judgment According to Law The Da Hing ship began unloading coal at the Beipiao Wharf the day before yesterday and will soon complete the unloading. The Antong Company also submitted a report to the Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications regarding the collision. Since both companies are Chinese merchants, the issue of future responsibility will be fairly judged by the Collision Committee of the Navigation Administration Bureau in accordance with the law.

Conditions for Rickshaw Pullers Renting Cars 155

The Public Works Department Board of Directors Will Consider Today

The Shanghai Times reported that the report submitted by the Shanghai Public Works Department Rickshaw Committee is currently being studied by a joint committee composed of the Police Committee and the Transportation Committee in order to submit a final proposal to the Public Works Department and the Board of Directors. The first thing to be considered is the conditions for rickshaw pullers renting cars. The most important recommendation in the Rickshaw Committee's report is to stipulate the maximum rental fee so that the income earned by the rickshaw pullers who rent cars can support their livelihood. Item 8 stipulates that the maximum rental fee is 80 cents per 24 hours, and for less than 24 hours, it will be reduced proportionally. The rental fee regulations will be formulated by the Public Works Department, and a clause will be added to the vehicle license stating, "The rental fee paid by the rickshaw puller shall not exceed the maximum amount approved by the Public Works Department." This section will be considered at the regular meeting of the Public Works Department Board of Directors this Wednesday, and it is believed that the date for the implementation of the new regulations will be decided at that time.

Chongming Murder Case Forensic Doctor Steams Bones for Examination 161

=Qiu Yinxiang's Nostrils Bleeding=

=High Court Designates Re-examination=

Yang Qiu Yinxiang, the pregnant wife of villager Yang Miaolang of Xin Kaihe Town, Chongming, committed suicide by hanging herself at home in May of the previous year (lunar calendar), with blood flowing from her nostrils. Her father, Qiu Chuanlang, filed a complaint in the original county, stating that the couple had previously been involved in a lawsuit due to not living together, and that she had been abused and injured after being forced back together, causing the blood to flow out. He requested that her son-in-law be dealt with. However, Yang Miaolang claimed that his wife returned to her parents' home in Ningbo and was stubbornly prevented from returning home by her stubborn father. During the lawsuit, his wife voluntarily followed her husband home. Therefore, her father hated his daughter for protecting her husband and would not return her clothes. Because he repeatedly went to get the clothes, he was repeatedly scolded and beaten, and she was forced to commit suicide. The original county verified that she had committed suicide by hanging herself. Her father refused to accept this, so the Jiangsu High Court designated the Shanghai District Court to investigate and re-examine the case. Upon receiving the order, the coffin was brought to Shanghai and sent to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for autopsy and re-examination. Yesterday, the coffin was opened, and it was found that the deceased's skin and flesh had rotted, making it difficult to examine. Therefore, the institute followed the procedures of the inspecting officials and used scientific methods to remove the bones for steaming and examination. The rotten flesh of the corpse has been removed, and then it is steamed and examined in a cage. It is said that it will take a week to determine the cause of death.

More Than 20 Electric Lights Are All Lit, But the Meter Is Not Moving 163

=Meifeng Electric Appliance Store Accused of Stealing Electricity=

=Zhu Shaoyi Describes the Investigation Process=

The Nanshi Huashang Electric Company has discovered that Meifeng Electric Appliance Store at No. 986, Yingxun Road Intersection, Xiaoximen Zhonghua Road, has been stealing electricity. The company's general manager, Lu Bohong, retained lawyer Wang Fuchang to file a private prosecution with the Criminal Court of the District Court, accusing the owners of the electric appliance store, Gu Quansheng and Zhang Quansheng, of jointly stealing electricity and requesting that they be punished according to law, as well as filing a civil lawsuit to jointly and severally compensate for electricity fees of 819 yuan, 9 jiao, and 3 fen. After receiving the complaint, the court issued summons. Because the defendants did not appear, Judge Zhang resumed the hearing yesterday afternoon. The plaintiff was represented by lawyer Wang Fuchang, and the defendants were represented by lawyer Liu Xiang. The first defendant, Gu Quansheng, did not appear. Only the second defendant, Zhang Quansheng, appeared in court and stated that he was 34 years old, from Changzhou, and ran the Meifeng Electric Appliance Store as a sole proprietorship. Asked if he co-owned the store with Gu Quansheng, he replied no. Asked how he stole electricity, he replied that he took over the store on September 2nd of last year and opened it on the 16th. The electrical wiring in the store had not been changed. At this point, lawyer Wang stood up and said that the plaintiff, Lu Bohong, had commissioned Qin Zhongying, an employee of the company, to represent him in court. He could explain the facts in detail. However, the first defendant, Gu Quansheng, was a craftsman in the company and co-owned the Meifeng Electric Appliance Store with Zhang Quansheng. However, the contract between the store and the company stated that it was Zhang Quansheng, etc. The official ordered witness Zhu Shaoyi to testify that he was currently the chief of the Electrical Affairs Section of the Huashang Electric Company. On the morning of February 5th, he was instructed by General Manager Lu to gather the staff of the Investigation Section and depart for investigation after stopping work at 5 PM that afternoon. He did not know where to investigate beforehand. At about 7 PM, he and the members of the Investigation Section, Chu Kexian, Qin Zhongying, Yao Xianting, and the craftsman, went to the Meifeng Electric Appliance Store to investigate. They saw more than 20 electric lights all lit. Upon inspecting the meter, it was not moving. After careful investigation, they discovered that a ground wire was connected to the tap water iron pipe next to the kitchen, which was evidence of stealing electricity. The current was flowing into the ground, so the lights were on but the meter was not moving. At that time, a craftsman in our company, nicknamed Little Wuxi, was also there. I asked who opened this store. Little Wuxi replied that he opened the store. I immediately interrogated him severely, saying that since you are a craftsman in the company, you should not do this, especially since the Construction Committee's rules are very strict. At that time, I was about to call the police, but he begged me not to report it to the police. He admitted to stealing electricity and wrote a note on the spot stating that he had stolen electricity and was willing to compensate for the loss (this note was submitted by lawyer Wang). Then I reported it to the general manager and, after carefully examining the employee roster, learned that Little Wuxi was the first defendant, Gu Quansheng, etc. The testimonies of witnesses Chu Kexian, Yao Xianting, Qin Zhongying, etc., were consistent with Zhu's testimony. Lawyer Wang also stood up and said that Gu Quansheng had been summoned twice but refused to appear. He requested the court to arrest him for strict investigation. As a result, the official ordered Zhang Quansheng to pay a deposit of 1,000 yuan and leave for further questioning.

Major Fire on Beijing-Jiang Road, Zhabei 164

=More Than 500 Thatched Houses Destroyed=

=More Than 2,000 Families of Victims=

At 11:40 PM the night before last, a fire broke out in the thatched house jointly occupied by Han Dianfa (55 years old, from Yancheng) and Huang Defa (51 years old, from Yangzhou) behind the Xiaochaguan on Beijing-Jiang Road, Zhabei, due to careless frying of oil and rice. The fire quickly spread in all directions. Since the weather has been dry in this city recently, these thatched houses are very flammable, so the fire quickly became uncontrollable. After fire trucks from various places rushed to the scene and tried their best to put out the fire, the area was too large and their efforts were in vain. The fire was finally extinguished at 1:25 AM this morning. The reporter immediately drove to the scene to investigate at about 8 AM. At the intersection of Gonghe Xin Road and Jiaotong Road, poor victims could be seen sitting and lying on the ground on both sides of Jiaotong Road. At the same time, the sound of crying was deafening. Even before reaching the fire site, it was known that the disaster was serious. Proceeding to the intersection of Jingjiang Road Branch Road, more than ten brick bungalows were seen destroyed. Further in, the auditorium of Dade Lane, named Tianwang Hall, along with more than ten brick bungalows in the lane, had been reduced to rubble. Looking north from here towards Jingjiang Road, what used to be the most lively market area, with Jiangbei shantytowns and brick bungalows arranged side by side, had turned into a vast wasteland. It is estimated that the disaster area covers no less than 30 mu. However, at this time, smoke and flames had not yet completely subsided. According to the results of the investigation, in addition to the aforementioned destroyed brick bungalows and a few scattered brick bungalows in various places, there were more than 50 Gu-family brick bungalows and more than 50 Tan-family brick bungalows, totaling about 150. According to a report from the Zhongxing Road Sub-station of the Fourth District Public Security Bureau, there were more than 500 thatched houses. Each of the above-mentioned thatched and brick bungalows housed two or three families, or four or five families, so the total number is estimated to be more than 2,000 families. The loss this time is estimated at 30 yuan per thatched house, totaling 15,000 yuan for 500 houses, and 100 yuan per brick bungalow, totaling 15,000 yuan for 150 houses. Other losses, such as shop assets and household furniture, are no less than several thousand yuan, so the total loss is estimated to be more than 30,000 yuan. Among them, some had fire insurance: Teng Yong Sheng Tobacco and Paper Shop had fire insurance for 500 taels, Jiang Yongfu Shoe Sole Shop at No. 16, Rengui Lane, had fire insurance for 700 taels, and Zhu Deben at No. 13, Jingjiang Road, also had fire insurance, but the amount is unknown. After the fire broke out, the fire starters, Han Dianfa and Huang Defa, were immediately arrested by the Zhongxing Road Sub-station and sent to the Fourth District. The number of victims is about 4,000 to 5,000, most of whom are poor people who seek a living day by day. Except for a small number who temporarily went to live with relatives and friends, the rest are homeless, living in the open air, looking emaciated and gaunt, which is heartbreaking. It is hoped that philanthropists will quickly find ways to provide relief, and the merits will be immeasurable.

Cargo and Ship to Be Salvaged Simultaneously

After the Sanbei Company's Wanxiang ship collided with the Zhaoxing Company's Zhaoxing ship, the Zhaoxing ship sank immediately. The various insurance companies underwriting peace insurance decided to carry out salvage and are scheduled to hold a meeting today to discuss salvage methods. The details are as follows:

Consultation Method: After the Zhaoxing ship sank, the insurance companies underwriting the Zhaoxing ship's peace insurance, including Zhaotai, Tiantai, Dahua, Huaan, Lianbao, Ningshao, Sincere, Taiping, Liantai, Yongning, Haihai, etc., decided to salvage it. The day before yesterday, they contacted the Shanghai agent of the Japanese Salvage Company, Mitsui & Co., and immediately telegraphed the Japanese headquarters to inquire about the procedures and salvage costs. It was decided to convene a meeting of the underwriting insurance companies to discuss the salvage steps after receiving a reply from Shanghai.

Salvage of Cargo: The passengers and cargo loaded on the Zhaoxing ship, including flour, piece goods, and grain, were worth approximately 120,000 yuan and were insured by friendly insurance companies such as Black Sea. Now, the friendly insurance companies have decided to salvage it. Yesterday, they contacted the Zhaotai Lianbao insurance companies that underwrote the Zhaoxing ship's peace insurance and planned to salvage the cargo and ship at the same time. A meeting was scheduled for today at the Insurance Industry Association to discuss the method. This is because separate salvage costs are very high, and if you want to salvage the ship, you must first salvage the cargo. If you salvage the cargo first, the ship's position will move deeply, and the salvage of the ship in the future will inevitably be difficult. If they are salvaged at the same time, the cost will be reduced and no difficulties will arise.

Arbitration of Responsibility: After the Sanbei Company's Wanxiang ship is repaired, it will continue to be dispatched and commanded by the Military and Political Department's Rotation Office. The Zhaoxing and Sanbei companies have not yet directly negotiated last night. The Zhaoxing Company decided to wait for the insurance companies to meet today and ask experts to legally arbitrate the issue of mutual collision responsibility. It is said that after the Shanghai Maritime Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications received the report, it has not yet decided whether to convene a collision committee to arbitrate the case.

The blows of the iron rod to the vital points were especially countless, so Gu Genda died of serious injuries on the spot. His confessions were all about not knowing anything. Therefore, the police station could not get any clues. However, according to the irresponsible words of nearby villagers, they said that it was due to oxygenation, so they turned against each other and staged this tragedy. Xin Da Xing Hotel, located at No. 178, East Xinqiao Street, Caishi Street, French Concession, was checked in by a young man at around 9 PM on the 4th. According to the claim, his name was Ma Amao, 18 years old, from Shanghai, a foreign goods merchant. He did not say where he lived. The porter led him to Room 5 on the third floor, paid the room fee, and closed the door to sleep. He got up at noon on the 5th, paid the room fee again, and opened the room for another night. Then he went out. At around 1 PM in the afternoon, he returned to the hotel and went to the room without making a sound. The porter thought he was sleeping. At 8 PM that evening, the porter, Wang Yongmei, from Taizhou, went upstairs to ask if he wanted to eat dinner. She knocked on the door for a long time, but there was no response. When she pushed the door, it could not be opened because it was bolted from the inside. So she looked inside from the window and saw Ma lying stiff on the bed, motionless. Knowing that something was wrong, she reported to the accountant to pry open the door and went inside to check. He had already died. Two small opium tin boxes and a piece of paper were found on the table in front of the bed. It was written in pencil, "I don't know much, I can't explain the circumstances, check Lihua," etc., seventeen words. It was then known that he had committed suicide by taking poison. The French Patrol House was immediately notified and sent detectives to investigate. An empty bottle, which seemed to be a medicine bottle, was found on the ground behind the door. The corpse was immediately sent to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch for autopsy. Because no family members were found, the Second Special District Court was requested at noon yesterday to send prosecutor Wang Ren and forensic clerks to the site to verify that the deceased had committed suicide by taking poison while alive. The porter, Wang Yongmei, was questioned about the circumstances of the discovery. It was ordered that the corpse be photographed and buried by Tongren Fuyuan Hall, pending identification by family members. The corpse was wearing a gray fine striped cotton robe, a blue cloth long shirt, a striped cloth short shirt, white fleece trousers, fine striped cloth cotton trousers, a black velvet skullcap, yellow thread socks, and black leather shoes.

Fisheries Protection Office Regularly Sends Ships to Patrol the Ocean 168

The waters of Wenzhou, Shengshan, and other places in Zhejiang Province, China, are concentrated fishing grounds. Since the beginning of spring this year, the weather has gradually become warmer, and the fishing season is approaching. The Fisheries Protection Office of the Municipal Bureau of Industry and Commerce believes that most of the fishermen's annual income depends on the spring fishing season. However, coastal outlaws take advantage of this time of fishermen's harvest to seize opportunities to rob. In order to protect the maritime safety of fishermen and prevent the above-mentioned outlaws, the office will dispatch ships Nos. 1, 2, 3, and Biaohai around the 20th of this month to patrol the waters of Shengshan, Shenjiamen, and other places.

Shanghai Telephone Bureau Converts City-Wide Underground Cables 169

Avoids Wind and Fire Damage, Protects Traffic Safety

Zhabei Implements Three Expansions, Pudong Adds Operators

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, in order to avoid the effects of wind and fire damage to the electrical wires and to ensure traffic safety, is converting all of the city's overhead poles and wires to underground cables. The third phase of expansion in Zhabei is actively underway, and due to the heavy call volume in Pudong, additional operators are being added. The details of these situations are outlined below:

Conversion to Underground Cables: The Shanghai Telephone Bureau, recognizing the frequent damage to overhead poles and wires from hurricanes and fires, which results in substantial annual losses, and understanding that even with the dispatch of repairmen, traffic disruptions for users are unavoidable, Bureau Chief Xu Xueyu proposed a plan to convert all overhead poles and wires in the city to underground cables for permanent safety. This plan was approved by the Ministry of Communications, with an estimated material cost of approximately 120,000 yuan. The purchasing committee ordered the materials from the United States and Germany and had them shipped to Shanghai. The bureau's planned implementation of the conversion project began with the South Shanghai Ring Road. Since the start of construction, the section along Min'guo Road has been completed, and work is currently underway on the Zhonghua Road section. The bureau plans to convert other districts after the South Shanghai area is entirely finished.

Zhabei Phase Three Project: The first and second phases of the Zhabei telephone expansion were completed one after the other at the end of last year. However, the third phase, which involves organizing the cross-border sections and adding lines and equipment, is considered more important and difficult. The materials for the third phase have already arrived. The project starts from the Zhabei Yongxing Road branch and extends along Sichuan Road to Diswei Road and the Jiangwan Road area, organizing the electrical wires and adding lines where there are no existing ones. The project is expected to be completed within approximately three months.

Adding Operators: The Pudong Telephone Branch has been officially established. The "04" switchboard connecting Pudong with the concessions has been transferred to the Concession Telephone Company. After the Shanghai Telephone Bureau took over the cross-border electrical rights in the area, the daily number of calls has more than doubled, leading to an unusually high call volume. As a result, the two 800-line generator switchboards are insufficient to meet demand. Therefore, the bureau has added two operators to serve the area. Shops and residents in the Pudong area are also enthusiastically applying for new phone installations.

First Special Court Prosecutor Investigates Committee of Xu Case Support Association 170

=Recognizes that the Association's Published Declaration Insults the Court=

=Huang Xianggu and Others Arrived at the Court but Denied Everything=

The Prosecutor's Office of the First Special District Court of Shanghai, regarding the Xu case support association's declaration published in various newspapers on February 22nd, which contained numerous statements insulting the court, believes that these statements obstruct official duties. A summons was specially issued, ordering the seventeen members of the association to appear in court at 2:00 PM yesterday for questioning. However, only Huang Xianggu, Jiang Chiping, and Shao Xubai arrived at the designated time. Prosecutor Zhong Qing of the Seventh Tribunal first summoned Huang Xianggu for questioning. Huang stated that he was from Jian'ou, Fujian. The official asked if he was one of the elected members of the Xu case support association, to which he replied that he had no knowledge of the association and was certainly not a member. The official asked about the meeting held at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce on January 16th, where he was elected as a member, as recorded in various newspapers. Huang replied that while his name appeared in the newspapers, it was likely a mistake. The official stated that the police had already investigated and confirmed that he was indeed a member, to which Huang replied by requesting the announcement of the police's investigation process. The official then announced that the addresses of the seventeen committee members investigated by the police all matched. The official then asked why he had not clarified the newspaper report if he denied being a member. Huang replied that he had been busy and had not paid attention to the newspaper reports until he saw it in the news today. The official asked if, since he had never denied being a member in the newspaper report, it could be considered a fact. Huang replied that he had never received a notification from the association. The official asked if he thought the Huang Xianggu mentioned in the newspaper was another person. Huang replied that it was. The official asked if he had not been notified of the meeting at all. Huang replied that he had not received any notification. Then, Jiang Chiping was summoned. Jiang stated that he was from Jiangsu, residing at 146 Julai Road. The official asked if he was elected as a committee member at the meeting on January 16th, to which Jiang replied that he was not a member. The official stated that it was recorded in the newspapers. Jiang replied that he had heard people say so and then looked at the newspapers. Although his name was there, he was in court at the same time. The official asked if the meeting at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce was in the evening, to which Jiang replied that he did not go. The official asked how he could be elected as a committee member if he did not attend the meeting, to which Jiang replied that he did not know. The official asked if he had been notified after the election, to which Jiang replied that the election was an offer, but he had not accepted it. Sometime between the 18th and 19th, he heard from others and sent a letter of resignation on the 22nd. The official asked why he did not publish a statement in the newspaper denying his election as a committee member. Jiang replied that he had not received any notification from the association, and after sending the letter of resignation, he had not received any notice. The official then stated that organizing groups and acting within the law is permitted by law, and the court never interferes. The court believes that the declaration issued by the association is problematic and needs to be investigated, so you and others have been summoned to court for questioning. Jiang asked to be informed of the declaration in question, to which the official replied, "As a member of the association, have you not seen the declaration?" Jiang replied that he had not paid attention to it and had been too busy to inquire about other people's affairs. The official asked if Jiang had signed the declaration before it was published. Jiang replied that he had not participated in it at all and had not even seen the declaration. At this time, Prosecutor Zhong pointed out the statements in the declaration that concerned the court, word by word, stating that these statements were insulting to the court, and asked if Jiang had signed the declaration before it was published. Jiang replied that he had not participated in it at all and had not even seen the declaration. Finally, Shao Xubai was questioned: "Are you also a member of the committee?" Shao replied, "No." The official asked, "Your name is published in the newspaper?" Shao replied, "Newspapers cannot be relied upon. To serve as a committee member, you must first be notified and sworn in by the association before it is legal. I did not participate. Later, someone told me that I was elected as a committee member, thinking it was another Shao with the same name. When I knew it was me, I published my intention to resign in the newspaper. Moreover, I was not present at the meeting on January 16." The official asked, "When did you resign?" Shao replied, "I expressed it in the newspaper," and presented a newspaper to the court. He further stated, "Since I have already made such an expression, I cannot be responsible." The court noted that since the problem has already arisen, everyone is mutually shifting the blame, always saying they do not know, so they were questioned again about when they first learned of the declaration. Shao replied about a week later, and he expressed his resignation after the 23rd. The official asked if since there was no formal statement, he had tacitly acknowledged the title of committee member. Shao replied that he had already made an expression. The official stated that it was too late. After questioning, the official ordered each person to leave and wait for review.

Major Fire on Datong Road This Morning 172

=Over a Thousand Thatched Houses Reduced to Ashes=

=The Fire Started from the Outside, Which is Quite Peculiar=

Following the fire on Jingjiang Road the night before, another fire broke out on Datong Road, Zhabei, at 0:25 this morning. Pei Yuezhu, a 46-year-old man from Yancheng who makes a living carrying water for the Laohu Society, lived in thatched house number 698 at the end of Datong Road, Taiyang Temple, Zhabei. Zhu Yan, a 25-year-old woman from Funing who makes a living raising pigs, also lived in thatched house number 44 at the end of Datong Road. At 0:25 this morning, just as everyone was asleep, a fire suddenly broke out on the rooftops of the thatched houses outside the doors of Pei Yuezhu and Zhu Yan's homes. By the time the two families realized it, the fire had spread throughout the entire house and affected the surrounding neighbors. Pei and others were awakened from their dreams and rushed out in a panic, alarming the neighbors, who fled in haste, supporting the elderly and carrying the young, causing great chaos. The cries and shouts shook the area. At the same time, due to the drought and the fact that the houses covering more than ten acres around the area were all thatched, numbering over a thousand, the fire spread rapidly. By 11:00 AM this morning, all the thatched houses had been reduced to ashes. The fire brigades from all sections of Zhabei rushed to the scene upon hearing the news, but the scope of the fire was too large and difficult to control. The fire was extinguished in one place only to break out in another, with little success. The flames reached the sky and were impossible to approach. As the reporter was drafting this report, the fire was still growing, and it was feared that over a thousand thatched houses would be reduced to ashes. Pei Yuezhu and Zhu Yan, from whose homes the fire originated, were taken to the Fourth District Police Station for questioning. However, according to the neighbors, the fire started from the outside, which is quite peculiar, indicating that someone had first lit a fire and then thrown it onto the thatched houses outside the door. At the same time, it was felt that the police facilities in this area were inadequate, otherwise, anyone intending to commit arson would not dare to do so so boldly, and the transmission of alarms could also be faster, without such a tragic situation.

Record of the Trial of the Notorious Robber Xu Guifa 175

=Committed More Than Ten Cases One After Another=

=He Was Willing to Do Anything, Including Murder and Robbery=

The notorious robber Xu Guifa, nicknamed "Rotten Foot Little Ningbo," and his accomplices Chen Jinchang, Chen Rongsheng, Zhang Qifu, Zhang Guibao, and Chen Kejian committed numerous major robberies in the British, Chinese, and French concessions. On the afternoon of January 30th of this year, at around 5:00 PM, French Concession detectives Lu Zhulin and Wang Rusong, Deputy Detectives Zhang Daorong, Bao Tan Liu Jinrong, Shen Jinshi, and Lu Jinxiang, upon learning that Xu was hosting a banquet at his home at 128 and a half Fuxu Road, inviting his accomplices, joined forces with Chinese and Western detectives from the Chengdu Road Police Station and rushed to arrest Xu and his gang of three Chens and two Zhangs, as well as Zhang Asan, who received the stolen goods, and Chen Shutang, a suspect (Xu Guifa's brother-in-law, who answered phones at the US Consulate), and Yin Tiancheng, a total of eight people. They then went to 18 Tianyou Lane, Haichang Road, Zhabei, the home of Chen Jinchang and Chen Rongsheng, and continued to arrest their wives Chen Ge and Chen Shi, and a woman named Huang Linmei, a total of three people. They found five pistols and forty-nine bullets in the house, and more than 400 yuan in cash on each person and in the house, and transferred them to the Second Special District Court for interrogation and investigation. During the rescheduling, it was found that Xu Guifa, Chen Jinchang, and Chen Rongsheng assassinated Shao Wenbin, the head of the Huahui, (also known as Groom Ah Liu), on Huage Road in July of the previous year, and assassinated Wei Qiliang, a native of Siyang, in Nanqianjiatang in October of the 17th year. From June of the previous year to January 29th of this year, they and the two Zhangs successively robbed Lin Bingyi, a resident of the French Concession (3 Le Fang, Xiafei Road), Wang Songtao (15 Ren'an Lane, Songshan Road, a section member of the Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance), Zhu Ningzhi (68 Hengqing Lane, Beile Road), Qiang Maosheng (3 Deshun Lane, Avenue Edward VII), Wang Xianling (20 Yuzhen Lane, Lafayette Road), Yuan Zhaoqing (1 Zhishun Lane, Pu'en Jishi Road, Xiaowan, who opened a rickshaw company), and six other families, stealing gold, jewelry, diamonds, and other ornaments, clothing, and cash. In the Public Concession, they successively robbed five diamond rings from guests and prostitutes in a Shantou Road brothel, as well as a pistol and more than 200 yuan in cash, and large sums of money from two families, one surnamed Mou, at 592 Lane, Baike Road, and 23 Lane, 640 Seymour Road, as well as a pistol. They also robbed 11,000 yuan from the Bank of China on Nanshi Road, and successively robbed the Public Concession, Chinese Concession, and Hua-India police outposts of pistols and other major cases, which have been reported in previous newspapers. The police have completed the investigation and have retrieved nearly ten packages of rough and fine fur, silk clothing, and other original stolen goods from various pawnshops (it is heard that three of the five diamond rings stolen in the Shantou Road brothel case have been retrieved). Yesterday at noon, the police escorted twelve men and women, including the Xu gang, to the Second Special Court, where Judge Zhang Chaozuo specially opened the Second Criminal Tribunal to try the case. The bailiffs brought the defendants to the court. After briefly asking their names, the police lawyer Fei Xizhen explained the police investigation. Xu Guifa, Chen Jinchang, Chen Rongsheng, Zhang Qifu, Zhang Guibao, Chen Kejian, and Zhang Asan were charged with murder, repeated robbery, and receiving stolen goods according to the criminal law, and the stolen goods and pistols were presented to the court. The police lawyer also stated that the police had found that the five defendants, Chen Shutang, Yin Tiancheng, Chen Ge, Chen Shi, and Huang Linmei, were not involved in the case and should not be prosecuted. He requested that the court release them first. The judge then ordered that the five defendants who were not prosecuted be released in court and ordered that the defendants be taken down and interrogated separately. Xu Guifa, Chen Jinchang, and Chen Rongsheng directly admitted to the two murder cases and the various robbery cases when questioned by the court. They shook their heads stubbornly, revealing a fierce and fearless appearance. (The confessions are lengthy and omitted). Chen Kejian, Zhang Qifu, and Zhang Guibao confessed that they were recruited by Chen Rongsheng to commit robberies. Zhang Asan confessed that Xu Guifa brought five diamond rings to him and asked him to sell them for him, and he resold them to Li Hongzheng, receiving 1,100 yuan. Xu gave him 30 yuan, and he was arrested for returning 70 yuan to Xu Guifa. By this time, it was 1:30 PM, and the victims of the case had not yet been questioned. The court adjourned the trial to the 13th, appointed a defense lawyer, and ordered the defendants to be returned to custody.

Con Artist Yang Letian's Fraud Case, More Victims Still Exist, Continued Trial Awaits Investigation 176

Last autumn, the con artist Yang Letian got acquainted with the wealthy widow Bao Xu (named Xunru), and immediately used threatening words, claiming that her luck was unfavorable, and her fate palace was full of disasters, so she needed to find a way to ward off the disasters. The woman fell into his trap, and over the months, she was defrauded of a total of 3,000 yuan. Recently, she finally realized and reported it to the police, who sent detectives to arrest Yang and bring him to the First Special District Court. According to the defendant's confession, he admitted that he had received money from Xu, but claimed that he had a special relationship with Xu, and that the money was definitely not obtained by fraud. The official ordered the defendant to be taken into custody, pending further investigation and questioning. After this case occurred and was reported in the newspapers, anyone who had been deceived by Yang Letian was deeply touched and thought about dealing with it. In addition, according to the police investigation, Lu Zhicheng and one person surnamed Zhu in this city were each defrauded of hundreds of yuan. Yesterday morning was the date for the continued trial of the case. The police summoned the witnesses and escorted Yang Letian to the court. Judge Deng Baosun opened the court to interrogate the defendant. First, the police lawyer Qian Jiu explained the investigation and stated that Lu Zhicheng and Zhu did not want to pursue the case because of the small amount of loss. However, this type of case is not one that can be prosecuted only by complaint, and even if the victim does not want to pursue the case, it does not affect the public prosecution. Therefore, it is requested that the witnesses be questioned and then postponed so that the police can reconsider. Then, Lin Zhixiang, a Ningbo woman who was Yang Letian's second landlord, testified in court, proving that Yang Letian invited women surnamed Wan to rent the remaining house at 8 Airen Lane, Avenue Aivenyi. Since Yang moved in, Xu Xunru also came every day at 3:00 or 4:00 in the afternoon and stayed until 3:00 or 4:00 at night. She often heard them laughing and talking in the room. China Foreign Famine Relief Committee Yellow River Disaster Agricultural Relief News 183

Call for Donations: Last autumn, the provinces of Hebei, Shandong, and Henan suffered from floods, affecting millions of people. Their homes were lost and their fields destroyed. They were only able to temporarily preserve their lives with the help of emergency relief. The suffering of these victims is likely beyond our imagination. The spring plowing season is approaching, and the victims lack seeds, farming tools, and livestock. Some even lack shelter. Alas, what crime have the victims committed, their hard-earned gains of the entire year being snatched away in a single day? If benevolent gentlemen do not rise to offer assistance, it is feared that none will be left. Under the current circumstances, they are not entirely without hope, as the Committee has already dispatched personnel to the most severely affected areas to investigate the needs of farmers, guide the formation of mutual aid societies, and lend appropriate amounts of funds to enable the victims to gradually restore their self-reliance. People widely praise the enthusiastic philanthropists across China who are donating millions to expand this agricultural relief effort. The victims place their hopes on the Committee, and the Committee should do its best to find ways to succeed. However, we must realize that this is not something that can be achieved by one person alone. It requires our united cooperation to succeed. Our Yellow River disaster relief campaign is being carried out separately in major cities across China, both in the north and south, either in the initial stages of organization or actively underway. Now that the Spring Festival has passed, we should strive to work harder to bring this campaign to a swift and successful conclusion, so that these more than three million victims will have the opportunity to rejuvenate and thrive.

Reports on Relief Efforts from Various Quarters: Nanjing | The Nanjing Fundraising Association for Yellow River Disaster Agricultural Relief has a promising start. The association held its opening ceremony at the Lìzhì Society on February 25th, following the banquet of the Fourth Plenary Session. Among the committee members present were Chairman Kong Xiangxi, as well as Jiang Jieshi, Wang Zhaoming, Dai Jitao, and Zhu Chen. Guests included Zhang Xueliang, He Jian, and over seventy others. Chairman Kong reported on the preparatory process, and Committee Member Wang and others spoke about the disaster situation. Subsequently, Chu Minyi and others put on a theatrical performance to raise funds. Donations pledged on the spot reached 20,000 yuan. The initial goal of raising 50,000 yuan has already reached two-fifths. This success is entirely due to the advocacy of the executive committee members Huang Renlin, Lai Lian, Hao Ruiman, Wu Zhenxiu, and Jiang Bengong, as well as the assistance of people from all walks of life. Reading Q&A

Reading and Writing (II) (Continued) 184

However, to achieve success in literature, there is another aspect you must pay attention to. Literary success lies not only in the form of the words but, most importantly, in the content. What you write should represent someone's voice and align with the demands and rhythm of the times. Does it genuinely have a considerable understanding of society? Is it intimately familiar with the lives of various social groups? For example, in your piece "Remnants of a Decaying Era," although in terms of consciousness, you expressed that "What is there to pity? This is the fate bestowed by the historical era," the result is that you still "take out all the few copper coins from your pocket." The atmosphere of the whole piece is still filled with a humanitarian sentiment, with a touch of melancholy. As for the subject matter, using the incident of "stealing a big cake from a cake shop and being injured by the shop assistant with an iron rod from the stove, and even with boiling water..." Even if this is true, even if we use the techniques of New Realism, I think using a cake shop assistant to represent the cruelty of all oppressors, if written factually, like reflecting in a mirror, would instead become a technique of Naturalism, making the adversarial aspect between groups even less clear; not to mention the "suggestion" that "everyone is a little indignant!" This is entirely a compassionate heart, not finding the truly angry target! (Or at least not very clear.)

Regarding the selection of material in "Remnants of a Decaying Era," it is not very clever—please forgive my bluntness—but this work is still a progressive piece. Its consciousness is correct. Currently, indeed, there are remnants of a decaying era. It is a pity that such good content has not found a more suitable form. This point is probably because the author still lacks understanding of New Realism and is unconsciously still influenced by Naturalism. Correcting this shortcoming, I think, is not difficult with the author's talent, as long as you pay more attention to several New Realist methods of expression.

Furthermore, in terms of expression, it is not just a matter of the skill of the words but also depends on whether one is familiar with and sympathetic to social groups. New Realism is not a slogan or catchphrase but the life of the masses, a record and guide in motion. For example, regarding the work mentioned above, it is just a sketch, not yet a novel because the descriptions of the characters and the composition of the surrounding environment do not yet meet the conditions of a novel. If we consider a complete novel, it would be quite difficult to write about an environment and characters that one is not familiar with. The result would be to walk into idealism, not only superficial and boring but also unable to achieve considerable success in the expression of the words. Therefore, we advocate that a new writer, in their efforts, should spend 20% of their energy on writing skills and 80% on content. We spare no effort in repeating that a New Realist writer should have a correct worldview, a correct understanding of the world, and a correct understanding of society. They should be one of the masses, not an observer or sympathizer; they should be familiar with the lives, wills, and demands of the masses and be able to speak for the masses.

At the same time, they should also learn new forms of expression and critically accept the legacy of their predecessors.

I have said too much. Regarding writing, I will stop here for now. Please criticize any inaccuracies.

Finally, I have the following two suggestions for your reading plan:

1. In the area of literature and art, you should read a few more famous works of literary theory.

2. Bukharin's Materialist Conception of History and Sociology is not good reading material in the near future. There are many errors in the book, which I will point out when I have the opportunity. For now, I specifically recommend the "Course in Dialectical Materialism" (translated by Li Da, published by Bigengtang) to replace Bukharin's work. (End)

Spring and Autumn

Children and Environment 187

— Tang Kun

Who can deny that children are like a piece of white jade? This piece of white jade must be carved to become a treasure. But who is the person who does this carving? Of course, it is the parents who are closest to the child. At the same time, a child's environment is also something that the child's parents can improve; or cause to become evil. Children intentionally pursue their lives according to their environment, so improving a child's environment is improving a child's life. At the same time, a child's current life is the foundation for building their future personality, so parents should pay twelve points of attention to their child's environment; and especially pay attention to the child's individual preferences, provide practical help for their development; and at the same time, provide guidance for bad thoughts and correct them with a technique. But one should remove the threatening method, because the threatening method only gives children a change in their thoughts; and cannot correct the errors in their thoughts.

Rousseau said in his famous educational work Émile, or On Education: "Do not punish the child, do not make the child apologize; because the child does not yet know moral evil, so hitting him and punishing him are inappropriate." This sentence is enough to make us a bible for training children. In fact, when a child is doing something, he does not consider whether it should or should not be done; so for the wrong things that a child does, the child does not bear a guilty conscience. If parents rely entirely on their own subjective attitude, a perspective that has been exposed to the ways of the world, to punish a child who has not yet seen the world, it will of course not be effective. Such punishment will only leave the child with an impression of being threatened, and of course he will still not regret what he has done wrong; and in fact, he has no chance to regret it. Therefore, parents should take a benevolent approach to teaching their children about their mistakes. In other words, use the child's own environment to make him discover his previous mistakes and be subject to a kind of conscience, which will prompt him to correct his previous mistakes.

Therefore, the responsibility for carving a child's piece of white jade rests entirely on the parents' guidance and teaching of a good environment; and one should try to avoid the venting of one's own will as a parent; and stand in the same position as the child to seek improvement.

On the Lake of Bacheng 188

— Xu Haowu

The steamer from Kunshan to Changshu passes through the first dock, which is Bacheng: Bacheng has a lake, which is called Bacheng Lake.

The area of the lake is not that wide. The lake is clear and lovely; the light waves are rippling, like the spring breeze blowing through the shallow grass.

Several boats are dotted on the south of the lake, with their oars laid aside and sails hung high; on the shallow beach, messy branches are lush and vibrant, swaying in the wind. On the other side of the lake, where black smoke rises, a steamer approaches from afar, gradually splashing waves onto our boat; thus, "Hello!" the two sides greeted each other, specially breaking the monotonous silence on the lake.

Looking to the horizon, green trees connect to form a large arc. In the sparse places of the branches, one or two bamboo fences and thatched huts faintly reveal a bay of roof corners: wisps of smoke, intermittently winding upwards.

The already bankrupt countryside, of course, is not enough for the "important people" to linger in their cars; but the inherent calmness and tranquility of the countryside—now perhaps we cannot say "happy and content"—the terror is something that the "important people" concerned with the gains and losses of chickens and insects cannot comprehend even a ten-thousandth of it!

To briefly mention what I know, Yangcheng Lake is famous for its crabs; West Lake has the scenic spots of Su Causeway in Spring Dawn and Three Pools Mirroring the Moon, which are admired by talented scholars and beautiful women; only this Bacheng Lake is located in the countryside, and its name is not heard throughout its life. The same clear water can cleanse the mind, yet the encounters are so different, is there also luck or misfortune among them?

The Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 189

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 25: Tearful Farewell to Loved Ones, Returning Home to Distant Garrison, Wind and Sand All Night Long, Setting Out to Garrison a Lonely City

When Zhao Ziqiang saw his situation, he also sighed and said: "Don't be a soldier, and if you are a soldier, don't get married." Tian Qing laughed and said: "Marriage!" Ziqiang said: "Rubbish! Marriage is a living worry." There were seven or eight people sitting in the company headquarters, and they all burst out laughing when they heard this. Tian Qing laughed and said: "Why are you making such a big complaint? Is there something you don't like about your beautiful wife?" Zhao Ziqiang said: "It's precisely because my wife is good that I say it's a living worry. Think about it, who wouldn't want to spend a few more days with their newlywed wife? But before I could get rid of her shyness, look, this telegram brought me back. In this way, it's nothing to me, but for a new wife, she hasn't even seen her husband's face clearly before she has to part with him. Isn't she sad?" Tian Qing laughed and said: "Old Zhao, don't say insincere words. Did your new wife really not see your face clearly?" Zhao Ziqiang laughed and said: "Even if she saw my face clearly, wouldn't it be better to be satisfied? Think about it, the biggest event in a person's life should be lived calmly. But we finished this matter in less than seven days. Who wouldn't be sad?" "Alas..." Tian Qing walked forward, patted him on the shoulder, and said: "The matter has already passed, and if she's sad, she's sad. What's the use of complaining like this? You've been here for so long, you should go see the battalion commander. I think he must have something to say to you too." Ziqiang thought, this is the right thing to do. He stood up, straightened his clothes, and walked towards the battalion headquarters. His battalion commander, Bao Fang, was standing with his hands behind his back, looking up at the sky. Suddenly, he turned around and saw Zhao Ziqiang. He smiled long ago. Ziqiang saluted and walked over. Bao Fang shook his right hand, patted his left shoulder, and said: "You are really obedient to orders. The telegram was sent, and you came right away. Is the new bride well?" (329)

A Glimpse of the Hangzhou Art Academy Exhibition 190

— Nanhai Seagull

Sunday! What to do for recreation?

Go hiking! In the vast Shanghai, there is not a hill in sight. Play in the water! The water of the Huangpu River is cold and turbid, unfit to wash my feet. The movie theater is crowded with dull heads; I don't have a ball to play at the sports field.

"Stroll on the street"! Go admire those truly "live movies."

Walking to the entrance of the Franco-Chinese Friendship Association on Huanlong Road, I suddenly looked up and saw the sign "National Hangzhou Art Academy Art Exhibition"! Ah! This is the "Palace of Art," the "Sports Field of Art"! I am a layman of art, but today I may as well serve as a person who ascends the hall and enters the room. The crowd ran inside, and I ran inside. The crowd signed their names, and I also signed my name. The crowd looked at the paintings, and I also learned from the method of villagers looking at notices to appreciate all the works arranged horizontally and vertically.

Beauty is in the eye of the beholder. Among these hundreds of beauties, I admired Sun Fuxi's Chrysanthemums, Xu Zhengzhi's Dogs, Li Chaoshi's Big Doll, Bai Shishan Weng's Water Birds, Lin Fengmian's Chinese Painting Sketches, the Wax-Dyed Magpie Plum, various industrial practical design patterns, and various poses of human body sketches...

The works exhibited at the entire exhibition are divided into Chinese painting, oil painting, watercolor, pattern, pastel painting, sculpture, and photography. Pattern paintings are divided into weaving, ceramics, lacquerware, advertising, interior decoration, and architectural decoration. The artists whose works were exhibited included nineteen professors and more than two hundred students from the Art Academy. There were a total of five hundred and sixty-two works. There were indeed many visitors. The art movement, taking the West as an example, is still in its infancy in our country. An exhibition of works from one school is like this, and if it is expanded in the future to become a group movement of artists from all over the country, it will not be difficult to create a grand spectacle.

If someone says that I am doing "voluntary advertising" for the art exhibition, I am also worthy of introducing him to be a "free viewer"!

In a Third-Class Carriage 191

— Fu Yizhi

Clatter... Clatter...

The train had been stopped at Jinhua Station impatiently. The snow, like goose down, was still flying down from outside the train window, and the huge eyes of a "dragon head" next to it emitted extremely strong light, reflecting on the raindrops on the glass window—the raindrops formed by the melting of the snowflakes, shimmering with fluorescent light. Unexpectedly, traveling by train on a snowy night would present such a more poetic picture before my eyes.

The ticket inspector came to the third-class carriage. A passenger in a seat near the door took out a piece of paper from the pocket of his "vest." The ticket inspector took it and only squeezed out a "roar" from his nostrils. Then, he grabbed him and pushed him towards the door... He only had a dirty outer shirt and "vest" that even a pipe worker would嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌嫌

Short Dream 192

— Bibo

In the fields scorched by the blazing sun, old Fu Gen still craned his neck, hoping for sweet rain from the heavens to descend soon, to revive the many withered and dying seedlings; but his daily hopes ended in disappointment!

He didn't have the money to rent a Western water dragon pump, and was forced to brave the scorching heat, walking to a small town ten miles away to borrow money from a rice shop he had dealings with; the result was another rejection!

Two kinds of painful memories assailed him, coupled with feeling some summer heat, he suddenly developed acute heatstroke halfway home; luckily, his neighbor saw him and helped him back home. He was also recently widowed, with only a clever daughter, Xiaomei, and a child who was only a few years old, who were both at a loss when they saw this situation.

Zou Si Sao, who worked as a servant in the large household of the Jin mansion in Shanghai, and who was envied by everyone in the village for being able to earn money, happened to return home at that time. She quickly mixed the prepared heatstroke medicine with water and gave it to him to drink, and sure enough, he gradually got better.

After a conversation, Si Sao unexpectedly lent the water dragon rental fee to Fu Gen without conditions, and also agreed to take Xiaomei to work together when she went to Shanghai.

The typical lifestyle of pleasure-seekers in the city was, of course, something Xiaomei, who had just left her village, could not have dreamed of; but Fu Gen was unable to pay off his debts because of the abundant autumn harvest and the drastically low rice prices, and with no other way, he had to write a letter to Xiaomei; but Xiaomei, however, had been targeted by the Jin family's second young master, who was just worrying about how to make his move, and seized this opportunity to coerce Xiaomei into selling her virginity.

It was not a big deal for young masters to take a fancy to a maid, but Xiaomei was still foolishly hoping that the master would fulfill his promise to marry her, because she was already pregnant.

Not long after, the second young master, who had once ravaged the village girl, was engaged to a so-called refined young lady; at that time, Xiaomei was tricked and intimidated by the master and mistress, and had to return to the fields with tears in her eyes.

Old Fu Gen was a man who cared a lot about face. When he saw his daughter and learned the truth, he fell ill with anger and died soon after; Xiaomei also gave birth to an adorable child during this period of grief.

In a closed-off village with rigid customs, people couldn't stand this kind of thing, and they all used Xiaomei raising an illegitimate child as gossip, spreading it everywhere. A kind of contemptuous and unbearable satire was more painful than poisonous arrows; at the same time, the Jin family, holding the grand theory that aristocratic blood could not be left outside, ordered their servants and Si Sao to entice and coerce Xiaomei, snatching away the child she regarded as her only lifeline.

In the process of unspeakable sorrow, Xiaomei took her younger brother to Shanghai to find her enemy, the second young master, but coincidentally ran into him in the car in front of the gate. He not only denied everything, but also sternly ordered the gatekeeper to drive her away. At this inextricable moment, her younger brother, who was casually looking at the scenery on the road, was knocked down by another car; at this moment, Xiaomei was heartbroken, but couldn't cry, and just stared blankly at the iron gate of the Jin mansion.

Sports News

Far Eastern Games Tennis Team: China to be Represented by Qiu, Lin, and Xu 193

Philippines Selects Chiavia et al.

Japan, Though Represented by Sato, Hyotaro, et al.

Still Possesses Strong Strength and Should Not Be Underestimated

The Far Eastern Games this summer are scheduled to be held in Manila in mid-May. The Philippines and Japan have already decided on some of their athletes. China still needs to wait for the National Sports Advancement Association's board meeting this Saturday before making specific arrangements. However, the preliminary selection date will definitely be in mid-April. Basketball preliminary selections are very active in North China. Japan has already decided on its basketball, volleyball, and tennis team members. According to Shen Siliang, honorary director of the Sports Association, China's tennis team will no longer hold preliminary selections and will directly send Qiu Feihai, Lin Baohua, and Xu Xinji to represent the country. According to news from the Philippines, they have also decided on Chiavia and Anben for singles, and Chiavia and Holly Sidan for doubles. Their doubles strength is particularly strong. Chiavia came to Shanghai last autumn, but it has been a year since then, and he should be regarded with new eyes. This time, Japan will be represented by second-rate players such as Sato Hyotaro et al., and may be able to put up a fight, but their strength is still strong and should not be underestimated.
